Commander BOGO
==============



 Posted in **Top Decks**
 on June 5, 2014 






![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/styles/auth_small/public/images/person/authorpic_adamstyborski.jpg)
By Adam Styborski




 Stybs has played Magic the world over, writing and drafting as part of the event coverage team and slinging Commander everywhere his decks will fit. 






Everybody loves a good deal.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/images/magic/daily/ct/2014/ct_wk22_302_cardart_moonlightbargin.jpg)
[Moonlight Bargain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Moonlight+Bargain) | Art by [Nick Percival](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?output=spoiler&method=visual&action=advanced&artist=%5B%22Nick+Percival%22%5D)



 What makes a good deal in **Magic** is getting something extra for the same cost as something else: 


* [Sakura-Tribe Elder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sakura-Tribe+Elder) gives a 1/1 Snake Shaman in addition to [Rampant Growth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rampant+Growth).
* [Wurmcoil Engine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wurmcoil+Engine), at just ![](https://web.archive.org/web/20161005045835im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/custom/wiz_autocard/wiz_manacost/manasymbols/colorless6.gif), gives *another* 6 power and 6 toughness of creature when it dies.
* [Indrik Stomphowler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Indrik+Stomphowler) gives [Naturalize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Naturalize) in addition to a reasonable body at uncommon.

 If we were talking about these creatures on Twitter (I'm [@the\_stybs](http://twitter.com/the_stybs)!) I'd be using the hashtag #Value. All three of those creatures are what I'd call "spell creatures"—each gives you something extra despite ample existing capability. It's this buy-one-and-get-one-free bargain that makes these kinds of creatures so valuable in Commander. 


Getting every last drop possible out of cards feels necessary when you have double or triple the usual number of opponents.


 That's part of what you find in *Conspiracy*, the multiplayer set for drafting you'll see at your local game store this Friday. As an aficionado of Cube (drafting) and Commander (multiplayer), finding a booster pack-sealed set filled with #Value has been exciting for me. 


* [Rousing of Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rousing+of+Souls) both fits into a token-focused deck (such as my revived [Rhys the Redeemed](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rhys+the+Redeemed) deck), provides helpful information about what's in who's hands, *and* draws a card to replace itself. (Spell creatures can be spells that give you creatures!) [Selvala's Enforcer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Selvala%27s+Enforcer) similarly draws into a card and information with a bonus attached.
* [Crookclaw Transmuter](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crookclaw+Transmuter) is a small body for Commander, but is a natural for messing with combat and even killing creatures when [Meishin, the Mind Cage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Meishin%2C+the+Mind+Cage) is around. [Jetting Glasskite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jetting+Glasskite) serving as a quasi-shroud shield enchantment on a beefy flying body isn't to be ignored either.
* [Morkrut Banshee](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Morkrut+Banshee) is removal—assuming morbid—on a stick. [Wakedancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wakedancer) is the reverse, giving you an extra creature for a low, low price.
* [Pitchburn Devils](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pitchburn+Devils) give out [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt) when they bite the dust. Paired with [Plagued Rusalka](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Plagued+Rusalka) and [Dictate of Erebos](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dictate+of+Erebos), cards like this help explain why black-red is such a scary color pair for Commander.
* [Sakura-Tribe Elder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sakura-Tribe+Elder) makes its triumphant return to booster packs, but [Terastodon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Terastodon) and [Wolfbriar Elemental](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wolfbriar+Elemental) are what you'd typically expect as green spell creatures for Commander.
* [Runed Servitor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Runed+Servitor) may look like a bad deal, but alongside [Nekusar, the Mindrazer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nekusar%2C+the+Mindrazer); [Notion Thief](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Notion+Thief); and [Uba Mask](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Uba+Mask), we all know how painful "giving out" extra draws can be for opponents.



|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| Rousing of Souls | Nekusar, the Mindrazer |

Creatures that give more are inevitably what fill my piles when building new Commander decks, and it's a clear trend that won't change anytime soon, given the piles that you sent in.



> 
>  "Spell creatures" surely is a fuzzy definition. I don't want to just staple [Naturalize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Naturalize) to a 2/2 deathtouch body. That's just efficient. I want ridiculous. I want my creatures to be ANY spell I want. That's the foundation of how my [Melek, Izzet Paragon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Melek%2C+Izzet+Paragon) deck is built. 
> 
> 
> 







#### Andrew's Melek


#####

99 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Steam+Vents)

















  

> 
> Basically, the goal of the deck is to cast as many instants and sorceries as possible. The problem with instants and sorceries is that they go away after you use them, unlike permanents. So my permanents help me get the most out of my instants and sorceries.
> 
> 
>  The creatures come in many groups. The returners are classic "spell creatures" that recur cards from my graveyard, like [Archaeomancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Archaeomancer) and [Charmbreaker Devils](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Charmbreaker+Devils). Then there are the duplicators, such as [Echo Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Echo+Mage) and [Djinn Illuminatus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Djinn+Illuminatus), that copy my spells to get more use out of them. Finally, Melek and [Galvanoth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Galvanoth) turn my deck itself into an instant-and-sorcery-slinging-machine. 
> 
> 
> —Andrew
> 
> 
> 




|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| Archaeomancer | Galvanoth |

Spells creatures that are creatures that get back other spells? We have to go deeper. Spencer did:



> 
>  I run a [Derevi, Empyrial Tactician](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Derevi%2C+Empyrial+Tactician) deck built on getting the most out of an army of ETB staples. My personal favorite is [Coiling Oracle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Coiling+Oracle), just because of the sheer versatility. Getting either a land or a draw for two mana is all well and good, but with [Deadeye Navigator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deadeye+Navigator); [Venser, the Sojourner](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Venser%2C+the+Sojourner); or good old "Roon Burgundy" ([Roon of the Hidden Realm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Roon+of+the+Hidden+Realm)) out, I can do it at least once a turn, giving me reliable ramping and/or card advantage for a minimal investment. 
> 
> 
> 




|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| Coiling Oracle | Venser, the Sojourner |


> 
> —Spencer
> 
> 
>

99 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Alchemist%27s+Refuge)

















  
 Creatures that carry spells that let you use the spells over and over? I mean, [don't twist my arm here](http://www.wizards.com/magic/magazine/article.aspx?x=mtg/daily/sf/192). 


 We can also just go as big as we need to blow up *everyone*, as James does: 



> 
>  My favorite commander deck is my No Pain, No Gain deck, featuring [Toshiro Umezawa](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Toshiro+Umezawa). My favorite "spell creature" in the deck is [Thought Gorger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thought+Gorger). Having grown tired of playing "safe" strategies, I designed the deck for maximum swinginess, no matter the cost. [Thought Gorger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thought+Gorger) is a beatstick that discourages killing it, and the downside is somewhat negated by Toshiro's fantastic ability. [Disciple of Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Disciple+of+Griselbrand) is my second-favorite "spell creature" in the deck. This deck plays very riskily, paying lots of life for card draw (I have paid up to 20 life for [Pain's Reward](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pain%27s+Reward) when I really REALLY needed a kill spell) and Disciple really helps offset the damage. Plus, getting rid of an unwanted [Abyssal Persecutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Abyssal+Persecutor) or lethal [Baleful Force](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Baleful+Force) is very helpful. Not to mention that saccing [Thought Gorger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thought+Gorger) to the Disciple is akin to an early Christmas. 
> 
> 
> 




|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| Thought Gorger | Disciple of Griselbrand |


> 
>  While not as exciting or flashing, my most utilitarian "spell creature" would have to be [Rune-Scarred Demon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rune-Scarred+Demon). Several of my win conditions require multiple parts to play successfully, and he is always there to lend a helping hand. Thanks to him, I have had many memorable victories with a combination of [Sadistic Sacrament](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sadistic+Sacrament) and [Mirror of Fate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mirror+of+Fate), or [Caged Sun](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Caged+Sun) and [Nirkana Revenant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nirkana+Revenant), or [Phthisis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phthisis) and an opponent's [Serra Avatar](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Serra+Avatar). Although it isn't the most consistent deck I've made, and I kill myself as often as my opponents do, it's the most fun and creates the most memorable plays of any deck I have made to date. 
> 
> 
> Here's the decklist.
> 
> 
> —James
> 
> 
>

99 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Nykthos%2C+Shrine+to+Nyx)

















  
As a fan of games that end with "Boom goes the dynamite!" it makes total sense the culmination of Demon shenanigans ends up with everybody biting the dust.


You can also be a little more selective in what "blowing everything up" means, like Stephen:



> 
> My favorite spell creature is a bit of a difficult question to answer. But I feel I can answer it nicely with a mono-green deck I'm working on.
> 
> 
>  It's a spiritcraft deck built around [Kodama of the Center Tree](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kodama+of+the+Center+Tree). Plenty of the cards could be described as "spell creatures," but it plays a few that follow your definition. If my board isn't getting repeatedly crushed, I can often turn every Spirit cast into a potent spell creature with the spiritcraft triggers. 
> 
> 
> 
> [Bane of Progress](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bane+of+Progress) is an all-star of the format, and the only mono-green card to destroy all artifacts and enchantments. With no spell to replace it, I guess it's my favorite spell creature. [Carven Caryatid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Carven+Caryatid), [Eidolon of Blossoms](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Eidolon+of+Blossoms), and [Haru-Onna](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Haru-Onna) have the three most powerful words in **Magic** written on them and stay to the theme. If [Bane of Progress](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bane+of+Progress) is green's nuke, [Acidic Slime](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Acidic+Slime) is the sniper. And what a beautifully crafted rifle it is. 
> 
> 
> 




|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| Bane of Progress | Haru-Onna |


> 
> Anyway, decklist below.
> 
> 
> —Stephen
> 
> 
>

##### Mythic (1)



1
[Forbidden Orchard](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BForbidden%5D+%5BOrchard%5D)


99 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Forbidden+Orchard)

















  
 Spiritcraft may not be at the top of your list of "**Magic** Mechanics That Create Impressive Value," but with the right creatures (there have been, and will be plenty more, Spirits made in the game) carrying the right spells, anything is possible. 


 Really, I mean *anything*. Zack even made the humble [Spore Frog](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spore+Frog) a force of multiplayer mayhem: 



> 
>  The first deck I think of when "spell creatures" are brought up is my Karador deck. Basically everything in the list has an ETB or dies trigger (or both!), making something like [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) a Swiss Army knife for all sorts of threats. But my \*favorite\* creatures? 
> 
> 
>  Being a long-game-minded graveyard deck, I have to say that [Spore Frog](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spore+Frog) is the guy I want to see every game. That little [Fog](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fog) Frog does a great job of "ramping" into my commander, helps me play politics with protecting life totals later on ([Gift of Immortality](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gift+of+Immortality) makes him an absolute nuisance), and is a bit of insurance against infinite-damage attacks (Prossh, Kiki-Jiki/[Pestermite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pestermite), that sort of thing). 
> 
> 
> 




|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| Spore Frog | Gift of Immortality |


> 
> 
> [Mikaeus, the Unhallowed](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mikaeus%2C+the+Unhallowed) is always a blast to resolve. Crafting the deck to have few non-Humans to get maximum value out of his undying ability feels very good, and he's a better [Cauldron of Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cauldron+of+Souls) with [Vish Kal, Blood Arbiter](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Vish%2BKal%252C%2BBlood%2BArbiter) hanging around, as well (that's an infinite combo that I like having in my back pocket). Add in how great he makes the evoke creatures ([Shriekmaw](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shriekmaw), I'm looking at you) and he just has the whole package. 
> 
> 
>  One creature in my deck actually came in, replacing a spell with the same effect, because recurring the enters-the-battlefield trigger is more straightforward than recurring [Eternal Witness](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Eternal+Witness) or getting lucky off of [Deadbridge Chant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deadbridge+Chant). I used to run [Pull from Eternity](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pull+from+Eternity) to help protect against [Bojuka Bog](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bojuka+Bog)-style hate, but then found out about [Riftsweeper](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Riftsweeper) in *Modern Masters*. When your opponents Path or Swords something like [Ashen Rider](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ashen+Rider), it is incredibly satisfying to drop it back in the graveyard to be cast again. This [Grizzly Bears](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grizzly+Bears) has earned its place in the deck many, many times over. 
> 
> 
> —Zack
> 
> 
>

99 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Orzhov+Basilica)

















  
Or, for those that take "spell creatures" to the obvious extreme, Matt pulled out all the creatures that could:



> 
>  I think my Ruric Thar Commander deck is the epitome of a "spell creatures" deck. I made a decision early on that I wanted it to be on-flavor for Ruric Thar as much as possible, which meant a lot of basic lands and a lot of creatures. My favorites include the creature tutors such as [Fierce Empath](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fierce+Empath), [Mwonvuli Beast Tracker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mwonvuli+Beast+Tracker), and [Brutalizer Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brutalizer+Exarch), with the latter pulling double duty as removal, too. Those set up for the bigger spells later in the game, including [Sylvan Primordial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sylvan+Primordial) (I am aware he is banned, but my playgroup is pretty lenient on that front) and [Terastodon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Terastodon), both creatures that can have a huge impact on the game all on their own. 
> 
> 
>  The suite of bloodrush creatures also are effectively spells. I rarely actually cast them, usually using them to either pull off surprise kills or to help Ruric Thar survive combat. I also have a host of creatures intended as removal for various permanent types, from an all-time favorite of mine, [Acidic Slime](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Acidic+Slime), to the one true piece of creature removal in the deck, [Gruul Ragebeast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gruul+Ragebeast). [Acidic Slime](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Acidic+Slime) is especially great since it often also takes a creature out with it when it goes—pure value. 
> 
> 
> 




|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| Acidic Slime | Gruul Ragebeast |


> 
>  Last, but not least, [Zealous Conscripts](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zealous+Conscripts) can be an incredible swing in tempo. I fondly remember stealing a friend's [Avacyn, Angel of Hope](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Avacyn%2C+Angel+of+Hope), bloodrushing [Rubblehulk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rubblehulk) onto her for something on the order of +15/+15, and then killing him with her. This deck simply doesn't work without a host of creatures that are also spells—everything from [Pelakka Wurm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pelakka+Wurm)'s lifegain to [Artisan of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Artisan+of+Kozilek)'s reanimation effect. 
> 
> 
> —Matt
> 
> 
>

99 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Forest)

















  

[Sylvan Primordial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sylvan+Primordial)—just like the  [conspiracies of *Conspiracy*](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?output=spoiler&method=visual&action=advanced&special=true&type=+%5B%22Conspiracy%22%5D)—may be banned in Commander, but between friends, you should still play anything your group allows. Also, who *wouldn't* want "Ruric Thar smash!" to play out as it ought to? 


But do you want ultimate power? Tyler tapped into the power of a God to fuel his deck of creatures:



> 
> Just like all my Commander decks, I can't choose ONE card. So, my Top 5 are:
> 
> 
> 
> > 
> >  5. [Mystic Snake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mystic+Snake)  
> >  4. [Gilded Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gilded+Drake)  
> >  3. [Coiling Oracle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Coiling+Oracle)  
> >  2. [Eternal Witness](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Eternal+Witness)  
> >  1. [Rishadan Cutpurse](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rishadan+Cutpurse)
> > 
> 
> 
> First, let me explain the deck. I LOVE green and blue. I wanted my deck to abuse "enter the battlefield" effects. It has lots of reusable bounce spells and permanents, so I can use each creature many times. So you're question this week for "spell creatures" literally IS my deck.
> 
> 
> 
> > 
> > 
> > **5. Counter creatures!** Bouncing Snake, Venser, or [Plaxmanta](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Plaxmanta), gives you reusable counters.  
> >  **4. [Gilded Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gilded+Drake).** Umm, I'll take your best creature. Thank you. By the way, I'll return the Drake with [Temporal Adept](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Temporal+Adept). Thank you again.  
> >  **3. [Coiling Oracle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Coiling+Oracle)** is amazing. Whether you want spell and get a land, or vice versa, you're gaining card advantage.  
> >  **2. [Eternal Witness](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Eternal+Witness).**  More card advantage. Add [Time Warp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Warp) and [Crystal Shard](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crystal+Shard) and you have a soft lock.  
> >  **1. [Rishadan Cutpurse](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rishadan+Cutpurse).**  By itself, it's not a big deal. In my deck, however, this is my kill condition, for everyone! My deck has many three-mana-or-less creatures that all have "enter the battlefield" effects, which works great with [Aluren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aluren). Add [Cloudstone Curio](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cloudstone+Curio), [Coiling Oracle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Coiling+Oracle) (for example), and [Rishadan Cutpurse](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rishadan+Cutpurse), and you bounce both back and forth to your hand however many times you'd like and make everyone sacrifice all permanents while drawing your deck and putting all lands into play. All during the end step! 
> > 
> 
> 
>  Side note: The deck's gone through many commanders. Momir Vig, Edric, and even Zegana. All work, but Momir and Edric painted a target, and Zegana never had a target big enough. Once Kruphix came out, it was settled. No max hand size! Save unused mana! [Deadeye Navigator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deadeye+Navigator) and [Cloud of Faeries](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cloud+of+Faeries) thank you! 
> 
> 
> 




|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| Momir Vig, Simic Visionary | Edric, Spymaster of Trest |


> 
> —Tyler
> 
> 
>

 While Tyler's deck is one that trips over my self-imposed power trigger, I know there are plenty of you who can appreciate the unbridled force [Kruphix, God of Horizons](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kruphix%2C+God+of+Horizons) creates here. 


Enjoy!


### What's Old is New Again


There were more decklists included this week since there were so many that covered different themes. Thanks, as always, for sharing what makes your decks tick. It'd be impossible to cover everything without your help.


 This week's question is much narrower: **What card (or cards) in *Vintage Masters* are you looking for to add to a Commander deck for **Magic Online**?** 



* Feedback via email
* 300-word limit to explain which card(s), and why
* **Sample decklist is requested** (does not count against word limit)
* Decklists should be formatted with one card per line with just a leading number, such as "3 Mountain"—just a space (no "x" or "-") between the number and the card name, *without* subtotals by card type (submissions that don't follow this rule will be ignored)
* Name and email required (non-personal information to be used in column)

 Not all of you try your hand at Commander online, but one of the surefire ways to get a game of **Magic** on from anywhere in the world is to log on to **Magic Online**. I know plenty of friends near—but mostly far!—who I wouldn't get to play with without a digital connection. 


 But more often it's just plain convenient to lounge at home, pizza in hand, and get a game in. With *Vintage Masters* packed with more than just the [Power Nine](/en/articles/archive/power-nine-2003-10-15-0), I want to know what you'll be keen to wield digitally. 


Join us next week when we go in under the cover of oversized power. See you then!
